      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Honiara_Ministry_of_the_Interior.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Honiara_Ministry_of_the_Interior.jpg/220px-Honiara_Ministry_of_the_Interior.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="89" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Honiara_Ministry_of_the_Interior.jpg/330px-Honiara_Ministry_of_the_Interior.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Honiara_Ministry_of_the_Interior.jpg/440px-Honiara_Ministry_of_the_Interior.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4751" data-file-height="1929"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Honiara_Ministry_of_the_Interior.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Ministry of the Interior
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Solomon Islands is a <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_monarchy" title="Constitutional monarchy">constitutional monarchy</a> and has a <a href="/wiki/Parliamentary_system" title="Parliamentary system">parliamentary system</a> of government. As <a href="/wiki/Queen_of_Solomon_Islands" class="mw-redirect" title="Queen of Solomon Islands">Queen of Solomon Islands</a>, <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_II" title="Elizabeth II">Elizabeth II</a> is <a href="/wiki/Head_of_state" title="Head of state">head of state</a>; she is represented by the <a href="/wiki/Governor-General_of_Solomon_Islands" title="Governor-General of Solomon Islands">Governor-General</a> who is chosen by the Parliament for a five-year term. There is a <a href="/wiki/Unicameral" class="mw-redirect" title="Unicameral">unicameral</a> parliament of 50 members, elected for four-year terms. However, Parliament may be dissolved by majority vote of its members before the completion of its term. </p>
      <p>Parliamentary representation is based on single-member constituencies. Suffrage is universal for citizens over age 21.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Head_of_government" title="Head of government">head of government</a> is the <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Solomon_Islands" title="Prime Minister of Solomon Islands">Prime Minister</a>, who is elected by Parliament and chooses the <a href="/wiki/Cabinet_of_Solomon_Islands" title="Cabinet of Solomon Islands">cabinet</a>. Each ministry is headed by a cabinet member, who is assisted by a <a href="/wiki/Permanent_secretary" title="Permanent secretary">permanent secretary</a>, a career public servant who directs the staff of the ministry. </p>
      <p>Solomon Islands governments are characterised by weak political parties (see <a href="/wiki/List_of_political_parties_in_Solomon_Islands" title="List of political parties in Solomon Islands">List of political parties in Solomon Islands</a>) and highly unstable parliamentary coalitions. They are subject to frequent <a href="/wiki/Votes_of_no_confidence" class="mw-redirect" title="Votes of no confidence">votes of no confidence</a>, leading to frequent changes in government leadership and cabinet appointments. </p>
      <p>Land ownership is reserved for Solomon Islanders. The law provides that resident expatriates, such as the Chinese and <a href="/wiki/Kiribati" title="Kiribati">Kiribati</a>, may obtain citizenship through naturalisation. Land generally is still held on a family or village basis and may be handed down from mother or father according to local custom. The islanders are reluctant to provide land for nontraditional economic undertakings, and this has resulted in continual disputes over land ownership. </p>
      <p>No military forces are maintained by Solomon Islands although a police force of nearly 500 includes a border protection unit. The police also are responsible for fire service, disaster relief, and maritime surveillance. The police force is headed by a commissioner, appointed by the governor-general and responsible to the prime minister. On 27 December 2006, the Solomon Islands Government took steps to prevent the country's Australian police chief from returning to the Pacific nation. On 12 January 2007, Australia replaced its top diplomat expelled from Solomon Islands for political interference in a conciliatory move aimed at easing a four-month dispute between the two countries. </p>
      <p>On 13 December 2007, Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Manasseh_Sogavare" title="Manasseh Sogavare">Manasseh Sogavare</a> was toppled by a vote of no confidence in Parliament,<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup> following the defection of five ministers to the opposition. It was the first time a prime minister had lost office in this way in Solomon Islands. On 20 December, Parliament elected the opposition's candidate (and former Minister for Education) <a href="/wiki/Derek_Sikua" title="Derek Sikua">Derek Sikua</a> as Prime Minister, in a vote of 32 to 15.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Judiciary">Judiciary</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Solomon_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Judiciary">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Judiciary_of_Solomon_Islands" title="Judiciary of Solomon Islands">Judiciary of Solomon Islands</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The Governor General appoints the Chief Justice of the Supreme Court on the advice of the Prime Minister and the Leader of the Opposition. The Governor General appoints the other justices with the advice of a judicial commission. The current Chief Justice is Sir Albert Palmer. </p>
      <p>Since March 2014 Justice Edwin Goldsbrough has served as the President of the Court of Appeal for Solomon Islands. Justice Goldsbrough has previously served a five-year term as a Judge of the High Court of Solomon Islands (2006–2011). Justice Edwin Goldsbrough then served as the Chief Justice of the <a href="/wiki/Turks_and_Caicos_Islands" title="Turks and Caicos Islands">Turks and Caicos Islands</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-TCCJ_97-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TCCJ-97">[97]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_relations">Foreign relations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Solomon_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Foreign relations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Solomon_Islands" title="Foreign relations of Solomon Islands">Foreign relations of Solomon Islands</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:%E8%94%A1%E8%8B%B1%E6%96%87%E7%B8%BD%E7%B5%B1%E6%8E%A5%E8%A6%8B%E7%B4%A2%E7%BE%85%E9%96%80%E7%BE%A4%E5%B3%B6%E7%B8%BD%E7%90%86%E8%98%87%E5%98%89%E7%93%A6%E7%91%9E%E4%BC%89%E5%84%B7%E8%A8%AA%E8%8F%AF%E5%9C%98.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/%E8%94%A1%E8%8B%B1%E6%96%87%E7%B8%BD%E7%B5%B1%E6%8E%A5%E8%A6%8B%E7%B4%A2%E7%BE%85%E9%96%80%E7%BE%A4%E5%B3%B6%E7%B8%BD%E7%90%86%E8%98%87%E5%98%89%E7%93%A6%E7%91%9E%E4%BC%89%E5%84%B7%E8%A8%AA%E8%8F%AF%E5%9C%98.jpg/220px-%E8%94%A1%E8%8B%B1%E6%96%87%E7%B8%BD%E7%B5%B1%E6%8E%A5%E8%A6%8B%E7%B4%A2%E7%BE%85%E9%96%80%E7%BE%A4%E5%B3%B6%E7%B8%BD%E7%90%86%E8%98%87%E5%98%89%E7%93%A6%E7%91%9E%E4%BC%89%E5%84%B7%E8%A8%AA%E8%8F%AF%E5%9C%98.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/%E8%94%A1%E8%8B%B1%E6%96%87%E7%B8%BD%E7%B5%B1%E6%8E%A5%E8%A6%8B%E7%B4%A2%E7%BE%85%E9%96%80%E7%BE%A4%E5%B3%B6%E7%B8%BD%E7%90%86%E8%98%87%E5%98%89%E7%93%A6%E7%91%9E%E4%BC%89%E5%84%B7%E8%A8%AA%E8%8F%AF%E5%9C%98.jpg/330px-%E8%94%A1%E8%8B%B1%E6%96%87%E7%B8%BD%E7%B5%B1%E6%8E%A5%E8%A6%8B%E7%B4%A2%E7%BE%85%E9%96%80%E7%BE%A4%E5%B3%B6%E7%B8%BD%E7%90%86%E8%98%87%E5%98%89%E7%93%A6%E7%91%9E%E4%BC%89%E5%84%B7%E8%A8%AA%E8%8F%AF%E5%9C%98.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/%E8%94%A1%E8%8B%B1%E6%96%87%E7%B8%BD%E7%B5%B1%E6%8E%A5%E8%A6%8B%E7%B4%A2%E7%BE%85%E9%96%80%E7%BE%A4%E5%B3%B6%E7%B8%BD%E7%90%86%E8%98%87%E5%98%89%E7%93%A6%E7%91%9E%E4%BC%89%E5%84%B7%E8%A8%AA%E8%8F%AF%E5%9C%98.jpg/440px-%E8%94%A1%E8%8B%B1%E6%96%87%E7%B8%BD%E7%B5%B1%E6%8E%A5%E8%A6%8B%E7%B4%A2%E7%BE%85%E9%96%80%E7%BE%A4%E5%B3%B6%E7%B8%BD%E7%90%86%E8%98%87%E5%98%89%E7%93%A6%E7%91%9E%E4%BC%89%E5%84%B7%E8%A8%AA%E8%8F%AF%E5%9C%98.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4493" data-file-height="2995"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:%E8%94%A1%E8%8B%B1%E6%96%87%E7%B8%BD%E7%B5%B1%E6%8E%A5%E8%A6%8B%E7%B4%A2%E7%BE%85%E9%96%80%E7%BE%A4%E5%B3%B6%E7%B8%BD%E7%90%86%E8%98%87%E5%98%89%E7%93%A6%E7%91%9E%E4%BC%89%E5%84%B7%E8%A8%AA%E8%8F%AF%E5%9C%98.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Solomon Islands Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Manasseh_Sogavare" title="Manasseh Sogavare">Manasseh Sogavare</a> meets with Republic of China (Taiwan) President <a href="/wiki/Tsai_Ing-wen" title="Tsai Ing-wen">Tsai Ing-wen</a> in July 2016
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Solomon Islands is a member of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a>, <a href="/wiki/Interpol" title="Interpol">Interpol</a>, <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Nations" title="Commonwealth of Nations">Commonwealth</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Islands_Forum" title="Pacific Islands Forum">Pacific Islands Forum</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Community" title="Pacific Community">Pacific Community</a>, <a href="/wiki/International_Monetary_Fund" title="International Monetary Fund">International Monetary Fund</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/ACP_countries" class="mw-redirect" title="ACP countries">African, Caribbean, and Pacific (ACP) countries</a> (ACP) (<a href="/wiki/Lom%C3%A9_Convention" title="Lomé Convention">Lomé Convention</a>). </p>
      <p>Until September 2019, it was one of the few countries to recognise the <a href="/wiki/Taiwan" title="Taiwan">Republic of China (Taiwan)</a> and maintain formal diplomatic relations with the latter.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup> Relations with Papua New Guinea, which had become strained because of an influx of refugees from the <a href="/wiki/Bougainville_Island" title="Bougainville Island">Bougainville</a> rebellion and attacks on the northern islands of Solomon Islands by elements pursuing <a href="/wiki/Bougainville_Civil_War" class="mw-redirect" title="Bougainville Civil War">Bougainvillean rebels</a>, have been repaired. A 1998 peace accord on Bougainville removed the armed threat, and the two nations regularised border operations in a 2004 agreement.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>In March 2017, at the 34th regular session of the UN Human Rights Council, <a href="/wiki/Vanuatu" title="Vanuatu">Vanuatu</a> made a joint statement on behalf of Solomon Islands and some other Pacific nations raising human rights violations in the <a href="/wiki/Western_New_Guinea" title="Western New Guinea">Western New Guinea</a>, which has been occupied by Indonesia since 1963,<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup> and requested that the UN High Commissioner for Human Rights produce a report.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-SBSMar17_101-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SBSMar17-101">[101]</a></sup> Indonesia rejected Vanuatu's allegations.<sup id="cite_ref-SBSMar17_101-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SBSMar17-101">[101]</a></sup> More than 100,000 Papuans have died during a 50-year <a href="/wiki/Papua_conflict" title="Papua conflict">Papua conflict</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup> In September 2017, at the <a href="/wiki/Seventy-second_session_of_the_United_Nations_General_Assembly" title="Seventy-second session of the United Nations General Assembly">72nd Session of the UN General Assembly</a>, the Prime Ministers of the Solomon Islands, Tuvalu and Vanuatu once again raised human rights abuses in Indonesian-occupied West Papua.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Military">Military</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Solomon_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Military">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Although the locally recruited <a href="/wiki/British_Solomon_Islands_Protectorate_Defence_Force" title="British Solomon Islands Protectorate Defence Force">British Solomon Islands Protectorate Defence Force</a> was part of <a href="/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_II" title="Allies of World War II">Allied Forces</a> taking part in fighting in the Solomons during the Second World War, the country has not had any regular military forces since independence. The various paramilitary elements of the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Solomon_Islands_Police_Force" title="Royal Solomon Islands Police Force">Royal Solomon Islands Police Force</a> (RSIPF) were disbanded and disarmed in 2003 following the intervention of the <a href="/wiki/Regional_Assistance_Mission_to_Solomon_Islands" title="Regional Assistance Mission to Solomon Islands">Regional Assistance Mission to Solomon Islands</a> (<a href="/wiki/RAMSI" class="mw-redirect" title="RAMSI">RAMSI</a>). RAMSI has a small military detachment headed by an Australian commander with responsibilities for assisting the police element of RAMSI in internal and external security. The RSIPF still operates two <a href="/wiki/Pacific_class_patrol_boat" class="mw-redirect" title="Pacific class patrol boat">Pacific class patrol boats</a> (RSIPV <i>Auki</i> and RSIPV <i>Lata</i>), which constitute the de facto navy of Solomon Islands. </p>
      <p>In the long term, it is anticipated that the RSIPF will resume the defence role of the country. The police force is headed by a commissioner, appointed by the <a href="/wiki/Governor_general" class="mw-redirect" title="Governor general">governor general</a> and responsible to the Minister of Police, National Security &amp; Correctional Services. </p>
      <p>The police budget of Solomon Islands has been strained due to a four-year civil war. Following <a href="/wiki/Cyclone_Zoe" title="Cyclone Zoe">Cyclone Zoe</a>'s strike on the islands of <a href="/wiki/Tikopia" title="Tikopia">Tikopia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Anuta" title="Anuta">Anuta</a> in December 2002, Australia had to provide the Solomon Islands government with 200,000 Solomon dollars ($50,000 Australian) for fuel and supplies for the patrol boat <i>Lata</i> to sail with relief supplies. (Part of the work of RAMSI includes assisting the Solomon Islands government to stabilise its budget.) </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">Administrative divisions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Solomon_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Administrative divisions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Provinces_of_Solomon_Islands" title="Provinces of Solomon Islands">Provinces of Solomon Islands</a>
      </div> 
      <p>For local government, the country is divided into ten administrative areas, of which nine are provinces administered by elected provincial assemblies and the tenth is the capital Honiara, administered by the Honiara Town Council. </p>

      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Human_rights">Human rights</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Solomon_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Human rights">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Human_rights_in_Solomon_Islands" title="Human rights in Solomon Islands">Human rights in Solomon Islands</a>
      </div> 
      <p>There are human rights concerns and issues in regards to education, water, sanitation, gender equality, and domestic violence. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/LGBT_rights_in_Solomon_Islands" title="LGBT rights in Solomon Islands">Homosexuality</a> is illegal in Solomon Islands.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Solomon_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <table class="box-Unreferenced_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Unreferenced" role="presentation">
       <tbody>
        <tr>
         <td class="mbox-image">

      </div>

      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Medium_shot_of_idyllic_villages_beach_near_Auki,_the_capital_of_Malaita._(10702263414).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Medium_shot_of_idyllic_villages_beach_near_Auki%2C_the_capital_of_Malaita._%2810702263414%29.jpg/220px-Medium_shot_of_idyllic_villages_beach_near_Auki%2C_the_capital_of_Malaita._%2810702263414%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Medium_shot_of_idyllic_villages_beach_near_Auki%2C_the_capital_of_Malaita._%2810702263414%29.jpg/330px-Medium_shot_of_idyllic_villages_beach_near_Auki%2C_the_capital_of_Malaita._%2810702263414%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Medium_shot_of_idyllic_villages_beach_near_Auki%2C_the_capital_of_Malaita._%2810702263414%29.jpg/440px-Medium_shot_of_idyllic_villages_beach_near_Auki%2C_the_capital_of_Malaita._%2810702263414%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="2448"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Medium_shot_of_idyllic_villages_beach_near_Auki,_the_capital_of_Malaita._(10702263414).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Malaita" title="Malaita">Malaita</a> island
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Solomon Islands is an island nation that lies east of Papua New Guinea and consists of many islands: <a href="/wiki/Choiseul_Island" title="Choiseul Island">Choiseul</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Shortland_Islands" title="Shortland Islands">Shortland Islands</a>; the <a href="/wiki/New_Georgia_Islands" title="New Georgia Islands">New Georgia Islands</a>; <a href="/wiki/Santa_Isabel_Island" title="Santa Isabel Island">Santa Isabel</a>; the <a href="/wiki/Russell_Islands" title="Russell Islands">Russell Islands</a>; <a href="/wiki/Nggela" class="mw-redirect" title="Nggela">Nggela</a> (the <a href="/wiki/Florida_Islands" class="mw-redirect" title="Florida Islands">Florida Islands</a>); <a href="/wiki/Malaita" title="Malaita">Malaita</a>; <a href="/wiki/Guadalcanal_(Pacific_Ocean_island)" class="mw-redirect" title="Guadalcanal (Pacific Ocean island)">Guadalcanal</a>; <a href="/wiki/Sikaiana" title="Sikaiana">Sikaiana</a>; <a href="/wiki/Maramasike" class="mw-redirect" title="Maramasike">Maramasike</a>; <a href="/wiki/Ulawa" class="mw-redirect" title="Ulawa">Ulawa</a>; <a href="/w/index.php?title=Uki_Island&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Uki Island (page does not exist)">Uki</a>; <a href="/wiki/Makira" title="Makira">Makira</a> (<a href="/wiki/San_Cristobal_(Solomon_Islands)" class="mw-redirect" title="San Cristobal (Solomon Islands)">San Cristobal</a>); <a href="/wiki/Santa_Ana_(Solomon_Islands)" class="mw-redirect" title="Santa Ana (Solomon Islands)">Santa Ana</a>; <a href="/wiki/Rennell_and_Bellona" class="mw-redirect" title="Rennell and Bellona">Rennell and Bellona</a>; the <a href="/wiki/Santa_Cruz_Islands" title="Santa Cruz Islands">Santa Cruz Islands</a> and the remote, tiny outliers, <a href="/wiki/Tikopia" title="Tikopia">Tikopia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Anuta" title="Anuta">Anuta</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Fatutaka" title="Fatutaka">Fatutaka</a>. </p>
      <p>The country's islands lie between latitudes <a href="/wiki/5th_parallel_south" title="5th parallel south">5°</a> and <a href="/wiki/13th_parallel_south" title="13th parallel south">13°S</a>, and longitudes <a href="/wiki/155th_meridian_east" title="155th meridian east">155°</a> and <a href="/wiki/169th_meridian_east" title="169th meridian east">169°E</a>. The distance between the westernmost and easternmost islands is about 1,500 kilometres (930&nbsp;mi). The Santa Cruz Islands (of which Tikopia is part) are situated north of <a href="/wiki/Vanuatu" title="Vanuatu">Vanuatu</a> and are especially isolated at more than 200 kilometres (120&nbsp;mi) from the other islands. <a href="/wiki/Bougainville_Island" title="Bougainville Island">Bougainville</a> is geographically part of the Solomon Islands archipelago but politically part of Papua New Guinea. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Solomon_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The islands' ocean-equatorial climate is extremely humid throughout the year, with a mean temperature of 26.5&nbsp;°C (79.7&nbsp;°F) and few extremes of temperature or weather. June through August is the cooler period. Though seasons are not pronounced, the northwesterly winds of November through April bring more frequent rainfall and occasional squalls or <a href="/wiki/Cyclone" title="Cyclone">cyclones</a>. The annual rainfall is about 3,050 millimetres (120&nbsp;in). </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ecology">Ecology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Solomon_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Ecology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The Solomon Islands <a href="/wiki/Archipelago" title="Archipelago">archipelago</a> is part of two distinct <a href="/wiki/Terrestrial_ecoregion" class="mw-redirect" title="Terrestrial ecoregion">terrestrial ecoregions</a>. Most of the islands are part of the <a href="/wiki/Solomon_Islands_rain_forests" title="Solomon Islands rain forests">Solomon Islands rain forests</a> ecoregion, which also includes the islands of Bougainville and Buka; these forests have come under pressure from forestry activities. The Santa Cruz Islands are part of the <a href="/wiki/Vanuatu_rain_forests" title="Vanuatu rain forests">Vanuatu rain forests</a> ecoregion, together with the neighbouring archipelago of Vanuatu.<sup id="cite_ref-DinersteinOlson2017_105-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DinersteinOlson2017-105">[105]</a></sup> The country had a 2019 <a href="/wiki/Forest_Landscape_Integrity_Index" title="Forest Landscape Integrity Index">Forest Landscape Integrity Index</a> mean score of 7.19/10, ranking it 48<sup>th</sup> globally out of 172 countries.<sup id="cite_ref-FLII-Supplementary_106-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FLII-Supplementary-106">[106]</a></sup> Soil quality ranges from extremely rich volcanic (there are <a href="/wiki/Volcano" title="Volcano">volcanoes</a> with varying degrees of activity on some of the larger islands) to relatively infertile limestone. More than 230 varieties of orchids and other tropical flowers brighten the landscape. Mammals are scarce on the islands, with the only terrestrial mammals being bats and small rodents. Birds and reptiles, however, are abundant.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>The islands contain several active and dormant volcanoes. The Tinakula and <a href="/wiki/Kavachi" title="Kavachi">Kavachi</a> volcanoes are the most active. </p>
      <p>On the southern side of <a href="/wiki/Vangunu_Island" class="mw-redirect" title="Vangunu Island">Vangunu Island</a>, the forests around the tiny community of Zaira are unique, providing habitat for at least three <a href="/wiki/Vulnerable_species" title="Vulnerable species">vulnerable species</a> of animals. The 200 human inhabitants of the area have been trying to get the forests declared a protected area, so that logging and mining cannot disturb and pollute the pristine forests and coastline.<sup id="cite_ref-fox_107-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fox-107">[107]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Water_and_sanitation">Water and sanitation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Solomon_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Water and sanitation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p><i>See also:</i> <i><a href="/wiki/Human_rights_in_Solomon_Islands" title="Human rights in Solomon Islands">Human rights in Solomon Islands</a></i> </p>
      <p>Scarcity of fresh water sources and lack of sanitation has been a constant challenge facing Solomon Islands. Reducing the number of those living without access to fresh water and sanitation by half was one of the 2015 Millennium Development Goals (MDGs) implemented by the United Nations through Goal 7, to ensure environmental sustainability.<sup id="cite_ref-Sectors_108-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sectors-108">[108]</a></sup> Though the islands generally have access to fresh water sources, it is typically only available in the state's capital of Honiara,<sup id="cite_ref-Sectors_108-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sectors-108">[108]</a></sup> and it is not guaranteed all year long. According to a UNICEF report, even the capital's poorest communities do not have access to adequate places to relieve their waste, and an estimated 70% Solomon Island schools have no access to safe and clean water for drinking, washing and relieving of waste.<sup id="cite_ref-Sectors_108-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sectors-108">[108]</a></sup> Lack of safe drinking water in school-age children results in high risks of contracting fatal diseases such as <a href="/wiki/Cholera" title="Cholera">cholera</a> and <a href="/wiki/Typhoid" class="mw-redirect" title="Typhoid">typhoid</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-reliefweb.int_109-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-reliefweb.int-109">[109]</a></sup> The number of Solomon Islanders living with piped drinking water has been decreasing since 2011, while those living with non-piped water increased between 2000 and 2010. Nevertheless, one improvement is that those living with non-piped water has been decreasing consistently since 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In addition, the Solomon Islands Second Rural Development Program, enacted in 2014 and active until 2020, has been working to deliver competent infrastructure and other vital services to rural areas and villages of the Solomon Islands,<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup> which suffer the most from lack of safe drinking water and proper sanitation. Through improved infrastructure, services and resources, the program has also encouraged farmers and other agricultural sectors, through community-driven efforts, to connect them to the market, thus promoting economic growth.<sup id="cite_ref-reliefweb.int_109-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-reliefweb.int-109">[109]</a></sup> Rural villages such as Bolava, found in the Western Province of Solomon Islands, have benefited greatly from the program, with the implementation of water tanks and rain catchment and water storage systems.<sup id="cite_ref-reliefweb.int_109-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-reliefweb.int-109">[109]</a></sup> Not only has the improved infrastructure increased the quality of life in Solomon Islands, the services are also operated and developed by the community, thus creating a sense of communal pride and achievement among those previously living in hazardous conditions. The program is funded by various international development actors such as the World Bank, European Union, International Fund for Agricultural Development (IFAD), and the Australian and Solomon Islands governments.<sup id="cite_ref-reliefweb.int_109-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-reliefweb.int-109">[109]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Earthquakes">Earthquakes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Solomon_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Earthquakes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/2007_Solomon_Islands_earthquake" title="2007 Solomon Islands earthquake">2007 Solomon Islands earthquake</a> and <a href="/wiki/2013_Solomon_Islands_earthquake" title="2013 Solomon Islands earthquake">2013 Solomon Islands earthquake</a>
      </div> 
      <p>On 2 April 2007 at 07:39:56 local time (<a href="/wiki/UTC%2B11" class="mw-redirect" title="UTC+11">UTC+11</a>) an earthquake with magnitude 8.1 on the <a href="/wiki/Seismic_magnitude_scales#Mw" title="Seismic magnitude scales"><span title="Moment mag. scale" class="rt-commentedText">M<sub>w</sub></span></a> scale occurred at hypocentre S8.453 E156.957, 349 kilometres (217&nbsp;mi) northwest of the island's capital, <a href="/wiki/Honiara" title="Honiara">Honiara</a> and south-east of the capital of <a href="/wiki/Western_Province_(Solomon_Islands)" title="Western Province (Solomon Islands)">Western Province</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gizo,_Solomon_Islands" title="Gizo, Solomon Islands">Gizo</a>, at a depth of 10&nbsp;km (6.2&nbsp;miles).<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup> More than 44 aftershocks with magnitude 5.0 or greater occurred up until 22:00:00 UTC, Wednesday, 4 April 2007. A <a href="/wiki/Tsunami" title="Tsunami">tsunami</a> followed killing at least 52 people, destroying more than 900 homes and leaving thousands of people homeless.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup> Land upthrust extended the shoreline of one island, <a href="/wiki/Ranongga" title="Ranongga">Ranongga</a>, by up to 70 metres (230&nbsp;ft) exposing many once pristine coral reefs.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>On 6 February 2013, an earthquake with magnitude of 8.0 occurred at epicentre S10.80 E165.11 in the Santa Cruz Islands followed by a tsunami up to 1.5 metres. At least nine people were killed and many houses demolished. The main quake was preceded by a sequence of earthquakes with a magnitude of up to 6.0. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Solomon_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Solomon_Islands" title="Economy of Solomon Islands">Economy of Solomon Islands</a>
      </div>
      <table class="box-Unreferenced_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Unreferenced" role="presentation">
       <tbody>
        <tr>
         <td class="mbox-image">
          <div style="width:52px">

      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Tetere_Oil_Palms.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Tetere_Oil_Palms.jpg/220px-Tetere_Oil_Palms.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Tetere_Oil_Palms.jpg/330px-Tetere_Oil_Palms.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Tetere_Oil_Palms.jpg/440px-Tetere_Oil_Palms.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5184" data-file-height="3888"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Tetere_Oil_Palms.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Plantation of oil palms near Tetere on Guadalcanal
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Guadalcanal_Field.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Guadalcanal_Field.jpg/220px-Guadalcanal_Field.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="149" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Guadalcanal_Field.jpg/330px-Guadalcanal_Field.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Guadalcanal_Field.jpg/440px-Guadalcanal_Field.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5184" data-file-height="3513"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Guadalcanal_Field.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Subsistence agriculture near Honiara
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Tamboko_Main_St.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Tamboko_Main_St.jpg/220px-Tamboko_Main_St.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="115" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Tamboko_Main_St.jpg/330px-Tamboko_Main_St.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Tamboko_Main_St.jpg/440px-Tamboko_Main_St.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5184" data-file-height="2716"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Tamboko_Main_St.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>One of the most important roads on the North coast of Guadalcanal in Tamboko
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Solomon Islands' per-capita GDP of $600 ranks it as a lesser developed nation, and more than 75% of its labour force is engaged in <a href="/wiki/Subsistence_agriculture" title="Subsistence agriculture">subsistence agriculture</a> and fishing. Most manufactured goods and petroleum products must be imported. Only 3.9% of the area of the islands are used for agriculture, and 78.1% are covered by forests making the Solomon Islands the 103rd ranked country covered by forests worldwide.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><b>Export</b> </p>
      <p>Until 1998, when world prices for tropical timber fell steeply, timber was Solomon Islands' main export product, and, in recent years, Solomon Islands forests were dangerously <a href="/wiki/Deforestation" title="Deforestation">overexploited</a>. In the wake of the ethnic violence in June 2000, exports of palm oil and gold ceased while exports of timber fell. Recently,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The time period mentioned near this tag is ambiguous. (January 2015)">when?</span></a></i>]</sup> Solomon Islands courts have re-approved the export of live <a href="/wiki/Dolphin" title="Dolphin">dolphins</a> for profit, most recently to <a href="/wiki/Dubai" title="Dubai">Dubai</a>, United Arab Emirates. This practice was originally stopped by the government in 2004 after international uproar over a shipment of 28 live dolphins to <a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">Mexico</a>. The move resulted in criticism from both <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">Australia</a> and <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand" title="New Zealand">New Zealand</a> as well as several conservation organisations. </p>
      <p><b>Agriculture</b> </p>
      <p>Other important cash crops and exports include <a href="/wiki/Copra" title="Copra">copra</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cocoa_bean" title="Cocoa bean">cacao</a> and <a href="/wiki/Palm_oil" title="Palm oil">palm oil</a>. In 2017 317,682 tons of coconuts were harvested making the country the 18th ranked producer of coconuts worldwide, and 24% of the exports corresponded to copra.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup> Cocoa beans are mainly grown on the islands Guadalcanal, Makira and Malaita. In 2017 4,940 tons of cocoa beans were harvested making the Solomon Islands the 27th ranked producer of cocoa worldwide.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup> Growth of production and export of copra and cacao, however, is hampered by old age of most coconut and cacao trees. In 2017 285,721 tons of palm oil were produced,making Solomon Islands the 24th ranked producer of palm oil worldwide.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup> The agriculture on the Solomon Islands is hampered by a very severe lack of agricultural machines. For the local market but not for export many families grow <a href="/wiki/Taro" title="Taro">taro</a> (2017: 45,901 tons),<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup> rice (2017: 2,789 tons),<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Yam_(vegetable)" title="Yam (vegetable)">yams</a> (2017: 44,940 tons)<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup> and bananas (2017: 313 tons).<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup> Tobacco (2017: 118 tons)<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup> and spices (2017: 217 tons).<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup> are grown for the local market as well. </p>
      <p><b>Mining</b> </p>
      <p>In 1998 gold mining began at <a href="/wiki/Gold_Ridge_(mine)" class="mw-redirect" title="Gold Ridge (mine)">Gold Ridge</a> on Guadalcanal. Minerals exploration in other areas continued. The islands are rich in undeveloped mineral resources such as <a href="/wiki/Lead" title="Lead">lead</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zinc" title="Zinc">zinc</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nickel" title="Nickel">nickel</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Gold" title="Gold">gold</a>. Negotiations are underway that may lead to the eventual reopening of the Gold Ridge mine which was closed after the riots in 2006. </p>
      <p><b>Fisheries</b> </p>
      <p>Solomon Islands' fisheries also offer prospects for export and domestic economic expansion. A Japanese joint venture, Solomon Taiyo Ltd., which operated the only fish cannery in the country, closed in mid-2000 as a result of the ethnic disturbances. Though the plant has reopened under local management, the export of <a href="/wiki/Tuna" title="Tuna">tuna</a> has not resumed. </p>
      <p><b>Tourism</b> </p>
      <p>Tourism, particularly diving, could become an important service industry for Solomon Islands. Tourism growth, however, is hampered by lack of infrastructure and transportation limitations. In 2017 the Solomon Islands were visited by 26,000 tourists making the country one of the least frequently-visited countries of the world.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup> The Government hopes to increase the number of tourists up to 30,000 by the end of 2019 and up to 60,000 tourists per year by the end of 2025.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><b>Currency</b> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Solomon_Islands_dollar" title="Solomon Islands dollar">Solomon Islands dollar</a> (<a href="/wiki/ISO_4217" title="ISO 4217">ISO 4217</a> code: <i>SBD</i>) was introduced in 1977, replacing the Australian dollar at par. Its symbol is "SI$", but the "SI" prefix may be omitted if there is no confusion with other currencies also using the <a href="/wiki/Dollar_sign" title="Dollar sign">dollar sign</a> "$". It is subdivided into 100 <a href="/wiki/Cent_(currency)" title="Cent (currency)">cents</a>. Local <a href="/wiki/Shell_money" title="Shell money">shell money</a> is still important for traditional and ceremonial purposes in certain provinces and, in some remote parts of the country, for trade. Shell money was a widely used traditional currency in the Pacific Islands, in Solomon Islands, it is mostly manufactured in <a href="/wiki/Malaita" title="Malaita">Malaita</a> and <a href="/wiki/Guadalcanal" title="Guadalcanal">Guadalcanal</a> but can be bought elsewhere, such as the <a href="/wiki/Honiara_Central_Market" title="Honiara Central Market">Honiara Central Market</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Barter" title="Barter">barter</a> system often replaces money of any kind in remote areas. The Solomon Islands Government was insolvent by 2002. Since the <a href="/wiki/Regional_Assistance_Mission_to_Solomon_Islands" title="Regional Assistance Mission to Solomon Islands">RAMSI</a> intervention in 2003, the government has recast its budget. It has consolidated and renegotiated its domestic debt and with Australian backing, is now seeking to renegotiate its foreign obligations. Principal aid donors are Australia, New Zealand, the European Union, Japan and Taiwan. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Energy">Energy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Solomon_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Energy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>A team of renewable energy developers working for the <a href="/wiki/South_Pacific_Applied_Geoscience_Commission" title="South Pacific Applied Geoscience Commission">South Pacific Applied Geoscience Commission</a> (SOPAC) and funded by the <a href="/wiki/Renewable_Energy_and_Energy_Efficiency_Partnership" title="Renewable Energy and Energy Efficiency Partnership">Renewable Energy and Energy Efficiency Partnership</a> (REEEP), have developed a scheme that allows local communities to access renewable energy, such as solar, water and wind power, without the need to raise substantial sums of cash. Under the scheme, islanders who are unable to pay for solar lanterns in cash may pay instead in kind with crops.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">[128]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Infrastructure">Infrastructure</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Solomon_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Infrastructure">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Flight_connections">Flight connections</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Solomon_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Flight connections">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Solomon_Airlines" title="Solomon Airlines">Solomon Airlines</a> connects Honiara to Nadi in <a href="/wiki/Fiji" title="Fiji">Fiji</a>, <a href="/wiki/Port_Vila" title="Port Vila">Port Vila</a> in <a href="/wiki/Vanuatu" title="Vanuatu">Vanuatu</a> and <a href="/wiki/Brisbane" title="Brisbane">Brisbane</a> in <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">Australia</a> as well as to more than 20 domestic airports in each province of the country. To promote tourism Solomon Airlines introduced a weekly direct flight connection between Brisbane and <a href="/wiki/Munda,_Solomon_Islands" title="Munda, Solomon Islands">Munda</a> in 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Virgin_Australia" title="Virgin Australia">Virgin Australia</a> connects Honiara to Brisbane twice a week. Most of the domestic airports are accessible to small planes only as they have short, grass runways. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Roads">Roads</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Solomon_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Roads">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The road system in Solomon Islands is insufficient and there are no railways. The most important roads connect Honiara to Lambi (58&nbsp;km; 36 miles) in the western part of Guadalcanal and to Aola (75&nbsp;km; 47 miles) in the eastern part.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">[130]</a></sup> There are few buses and these do not circulate according to a fixed timetable. In Honiara there is no bus terminus. The most important bus stop is in front of the Central Market. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ferries">Ferries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Solomon_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Ferries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Most of the islands can be reached by ferry from Honiara. There is a daily connection from Honiara to Auki via Tulagi by a high speed catamaran. </p>

       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The majority of Solomon Islanders are ethnically <a href="/wiki/Melanesian" class="mw-redirect" title="Melanesian">Melanesian</a> (95.3%). <a href="/wiki/Polynesians" title="Polynesians">Polynesian</a> (3.1%) and <a href="/wiki/Micronesian_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Micronesian people">Micronesian</a> (1.2%) are the two other significant groups.<sup id="cite_ref-Country_profile:_Solomon_Islands_131-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Country_profile:_Solomon_Islands-131">[131]</a></sup> There are a few thousand ethnic <a href="/wiki/Overseas_Chinese" title="Overseas Chinese">Chinese</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC_81-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC-81">[81]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Solomon_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Languages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Solomon_Islands" class="mw-redirect" title="Languages of Solomon Islands">Languages of Solomon Islands</a>
      </div> 
      <p>While English is the official language, only 1–2% of the population are able to communicate fluently in English. However, an English creole, Solomons <a href="/wiki/Pijin" class="mw-redirect" title="Pijin">Pijin</a>, is a <i>de facto</i> <a href="/wiki/Lingua_franca" title="Lingua franca">lingua franca</a> of the country spoken by the majority of the population, along with local tribal languages. Pijin is closely related to <a href="/wiki/Tok_Pisin" title="Tok Pisin">Tok Pisin</a> spoken in Papua New Guinea. </p>
      <p>The number of local languages listed for Solomon Islands is 74, of which 70 are living languages and 4 are extinct, according to <i>Ethnologue, Languages of the World</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">[132]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Western_Oceanic_languages" title="Western Oceanic languages">Western Oceanic languages</a> (predominantly of the <a href="/wiki/Southeast_Solomonic_languages" title="Southeast Solomonic languages">Southeast Solomonic group</a>) are spoken on the central islands. <a href="/wiki/Polynesian_languages" title="Polynesian languages">Polynesian languages</a> are spoken on <a href="/wiki/Rennell_Island" title="Rennell Island">Rennell</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bellona_Island" title="Bellona Island">Bellona</a> to the south, <a href="/wiki/Tikopia" title="Tikopia">Tikopia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Anuta" title="Anuta">Anuta</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fatutaka" title="Fatutaka">Fatutaka</a> to the far east, <a href="/wiki/Sikaiana" title="Sikaiana">Sikaiana</a> to the north east, and Luaniua to the north (<a href="/wiki/Ontong_Java_Atoll" title="Ontong Java Atoll">Ontong Java Atoll</a>, also known as <a href="/wiki/Lord_Howe_Atoll" class="mw-redirect" title="Lord Howe Atoll">Lord Howe Atoll</a>). The immigrant population of <a href="/wiki/Gilbertese_language" title="Gilbertese language">Gilbertese</a> (<a href="/wiki/Kiribati" title="Kiribati">I-Kiribati</a>) speaks an <a href="/wiki/Oceanic_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Oceanic language">Oceanic language</a>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Solomon_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Solomon_Islands" title="Religion in Solomon Islands">Religion in Solomon Islands</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Tanagai_Church.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Tanagai_Church.jpg/220px-Tanagai_Church.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="149" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Tanagai_Church.jpg/330px-Tanagai_Church.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Tanagai_Church.jpg/440px-Tanagai_Church.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5027" data-file-height="3397"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Tanagai_Church.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Catholic Church in Tanagai on Guadalcanal
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The religion of Solomon Islands is mainly Christian (comprising about 92% of the population). The main Christian denominations are: the Anglican <a href="/wiki/Church_of_the_Province_of_Melanesia" class="mw-redirect" title="Church of the Province of Melanesia">Church of Melanesia</a> (35%), <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church_in_Solomon_Islands" title="Catholic Church in Solomon Islands">Catholic Church</a> (19%), <a href="/wiki/South_Seas_Evangelical_Church" title="South Seas Evangelical Church">South Seas Evangelical Church</a> (17%), <a href="/wiki/United_Church_in_Papua_New_Guinea_and_the_Solomon_Islands" class="mw-redirect" title="United Church in Papua New Guinea and the Solomon Islands">United Church in Papua New Guinea and the Solomon Islands</a> (11%) and <a href="/wiki/Seventh-day_Adventist_Church" title="Seventh-day Adventist Church">Seventh-day Adventist</a> (10%). Other Christian denominations are <a href="/wiki/Jehovah%27s_Witnesses" title="Jehovah's Witnesses">Jehovah's Witnesses</a>, New Apostolic Church (80 churches) and <a href="/wiki/The_Church_of_Jesus_Christ_of_Latter-day_Saints" title="The Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints">The Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints</a> (LDS Church). </p>
      <p>Another 5% adhere to aboriginal beliefs. The remaining adhere to <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%CA%BC%C3%AD_Faith" title="Baháʼí Faith">Baháʼí Faith</a>. According to the most recent reports, <a href="/wiki/Islam_in_Solomon_Islands" class="mw-redirect" title="Islam in Solomon Islands">Islam in Solomon Islands</a> is made up of approximately 350 Muslims,<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">[133]</a></sup> including members of the <a href="/wiki/Ahmadiyya_Muslim_Community" class="mw-redirect" title="Ahmadiyya Muslim Community">Ahmadiyya Muslim Community</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">[134]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Health">Health</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Solomon_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Health">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Female life expectancy at birth was at 66.7 years and male life expectancy at birth at 64.9 in 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-hdrstats.undp.org_135-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hdrstats.undp.org-135">[135]</a></sup> 1990–1995 fertility rate was at 5.5 births per woman.<sup id="cite_ref-hdrstats.undp.org_135-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hdrstats.undp.org-135">[135]</a></sup> Government expenditure on health per capita was at US$99 (PPP).<sup id="cite_ref-hdrstats.undp.org_135-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hdrstats.undp.org-135">[135]</a></sup> Healthy life expectancy at birth is at 60 years.<sup id="cite_ref-hdrstats.undp.org_135-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hdrstats.undp.org-135">[135]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Blond hair occurs in 10% of the population in the islands.<sup id="cite_ref-Loury_136-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Loury-136">[136]</a></sup> After years of questions, studies have resulted in the better understanding of the blond gene. The findings show that the blond hair trait is due to an amino acid change of protein <a href="/wiki/TYRP1" title="TYRP1">TYRP1</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">[137]</a></sup> This accounts for the highest occurrence of blond hair outside of European influence in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">[138]</a></sup> While 10% of Solomon Islanders display the blond phenotype, about 26% of the population carry the recessive trait for it as well.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">[139]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Communicable_diseases">Communicable diseases</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Solomon_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Communicable diseases">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>About 35% deaths occurred in 2008 due to communicable diseases and maternal, perinatal, and nutritional conditions.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_140-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-140">[140]</a></sup> Solomon Islands had 13 cumulative HIV cases from 1994 to 2009 and between 2000 and 2011 confirmed malaria cases decreased steadily.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_140-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-140">[140]</a></sup> In 2017 lower respiratory infections accounted for 11.18%, neonatal disorders for 3.59%, STI (excluding HIV) for 2.9% of total deaths.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_141-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-141">[141]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Noncommunicable_diseases">Noncommunicable diseases</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Solomon_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Noncommunicable diseases">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>Noncommunicable diseases (NCDs) are prime causes of deaths in pacific islands, responsible for 60% deaths in Solomon Islands.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">[142]</a></sup> Premature mortality from NCDs was 1900 in 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">[143]</a></sup> Ischemic heart disease, stroke and diabetes were the main causes of mortality due to NCDs in 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_141-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-141">[141]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Sustainable_development_goals_and_Solomon_Islands">Sustainable development goals and Solomon Islands</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Solomon_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Sustainable development goals and Solomon Islands">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5> 
      <p>Over last two decades Solomon Islands has achieved many goals in health outcomes and moving towards fulfilling universal health coverage.<sup id="cite_ref-:2_144-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-144">[144]</a></sup> Identifying and treating NCDs, addressing manpower shortage in health sector, improving the availability of treatment facilities in all health care centers are the new priorities of Solomon Islands.<sup id="cite_ref-:2_144-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-144">[144]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Solomon_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Fenualoa_Tuo_school_children.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Fenualoa_Tuo_school_children.jpg/220px-Fenualoa_Tuo_school_children.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Fenualoa_Tuo_school_children.jpg/330px-Fenualoa_Tuo_school_children.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Fenualoa_Tuo_school_children.jpg/440px-Fenualoa_Tuo_school_children.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Fenualoa_Tuo_school_children.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Children at the school in Tuo village, <a href="/wiki/Fenualoa" title="Fenualoa">Fenualoa</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Honiara_Kindergarden.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Honiara_Kindergarden.jpg/220px-Honiara_Kindergarden.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Honiara_Kindergarden.jpg/330px-Honiara_Kindergarden.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Honiara_Kindergarden.jpg/440px-Honiara_Kindergarden.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5184" data-file-height="3886"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Honiara_Kindergarden.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Kindergarten in Honiara
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Tanagai_Schule.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Tanagai_Schule.jpg/220px-Tanagai_Schule.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="132" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Tanagai_Schule.jpg/330px-Tanagai_Schule.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Tanagai_Schule.jpg/440px-Tanagai_Schule.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5184" data-file-height="3116"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Tanagai_Schule.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>School in Tanagai on Guadalcanal
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Education in Solomon Islands is not compulsory, and only 60 percent of school-age children have access to primary education.<sup id="cite_ref-ilab_145-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ilab-145">[145]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-spc.int_146-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-spc.int-146">[146]</a></sup> There are kindergartens in various places, e.g. in the capital, but they are not free. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:University_of_the_South_Pacific,_Honiara.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/University_of_the_South_Pacific%2C_Honiara.jpg/220px-University_of_the_South_Pacific%2C_Honiara.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/University_of_the_South_Pacific%2C_Honiara.jpg/330px-University_of_the_South_Pacific%2C_Honiara.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/University_of_the_South_Pacific%2C_Honiara.jpg/440px-University_of_the_South_Pacific%2C_Honiara.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5184" data-file-height="3888"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:University_of_the_South_Pacific,_Honiara.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Campus of the University of the South Pacific in Honiara
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>From 1990 to 1994, the gross primary school enrolment rose from 84.5 percent to 96.6 percent.<sup id="cite_ref-ilab_145-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ilab-145">[145]</a></sup> Primary school attendance rates were unavailable for Solomon Islands as of 2001.<sup id="cite_ref-ilab_145-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ilab-145">[145]</a></sup> While enrolment rates indicate a level of commitment to education, they do not always reflect children's participation in school.<sup id="cite_ref-ilab_145-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ilab-145">[145]</a></sup> The Department of Education and Human Resource Development efforts and plans to expand educational facilities and increase enrolment. However, these actions have been hindered by a lack of government funding, misguided teacher training programs, poor co-ordination of programs, and a failure of the government to pay teachers.<sup id="cite_ref-ilab_145-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ilab-145">[145]</a></sup> The percentage of the government's budget allocated to education was 9.7 percent in 1998, down from 13.2 percent in 1990.<sup id="cite_ref-ilab_145-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ilab-145">[145]</a></sup> Male educational attainment tends to be higher than female educational attainment.<sup id="cite_ref-spc.int_146-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-spc.int-146">[146]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/University_of_the_South_Pacific" title="University of the South Pacific">University of the South Pacific</a> has a Campus at <a href="/wiki/Guadalcanal" title="Guadalcanal">Guadalcanal</a> as a foothold in the country while this University has established by Papua New Guinea.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">[147]</a></sup> The literacy rate of the adult population amounted to 84.1% in 2015 (men 88.9%, women 79.23%).<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">[148]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Solomon_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Solomon_Islands" title="Culture of Solomon Islands">Culture of Solomon Islands</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Honiara_National_Museum.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Honiara_National_Museum.jpg/220px-Honiara_National_Museum.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="142" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Honiara_National_Museum.jpg/330px-Honiara_National_Museum.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Honiara_National_Museum.jpg/440px-Honiara_National_Museum.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4729" data-file-height="3062"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Honiara_National_Museum.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Traditional painting and wood carving in the National Museum in Honiara
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Solomon_Islands" title="Culture of Solomon Islands">culture of Solomon Islands</a> reflects the extent of the differentiation and diversity among the groups living within the <a href="/wiki/Solomon_Islands_(archipelago)" title="Solomon Islands (archipelago)">Solomon Islands archipelago</a>, which lies within <a href="/wiki/Melanesia" title="Melanesia">Melanesia</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Ocean" title="Pacific Ocean">Pacific Ocean</a>, with the peoples distinguished by island, language, topography, and geography. The cultural area includes the nation state of Solomon Islands and the <a href="/wiki/Bougainville_Island" title="Bougainville Island">Bougainville Island</a>, which is a part of <a href="/wiki/Papua_New_Guinea" title="Papua New Guinea">Papua New Guinea</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">[149]</a></sup> Solomon Islands includes some <a href="/wiki/Polynesian_culture" title="Polynesian culture">culturally Polynesian</a> societies which lie outside the main region of Polynesian influence, known as the <a href="/wiki/Polynesian_Triangle" title="Polynesian Triangle">Polynesian Triangle</a>. There are seven <a href="/wiki/Polynesian_outliers" class="mw-redirect" title="Polynesian outliers">Polynesian outliers</a> within the Solomon Islands: <a href="/wiki/Anuta" title="Anuta">Anuta</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bellona_Island" title="Bellona Island">Bellona</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ontong_Java" class="mw-redirect" title="Ontong Java">Ontong Java</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rennell_Island" title="Rennell Island">Rennell</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sikaiana" title="Sikaiana">Sikaiana</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tikopia" title="Tikopia">Tikopia</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Vaeakau-Taumako" class="mw-redirect" title="Vaeakau-Taumako">Vaeakau-Taumako</a>. Solomon Islands arts and crafts cover a wide range of woven objects, carved wood, stone and shell artefacts in styles specific to different provinces.&nbsp;: </p>

       <li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px">
        <div style="width: 155px">
