      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Gender_inequality_and_domestic_violence">Gender inequality and domestic violence</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Solomon_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Gender inequality and domestic violence">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Solomon Islands has one of the highest rates of family and sexual violence (FSV) in the world, with 64% of women aged 15–49 having reported physical and/or sexual abuse by a partner.<sup id="cite_ref-Ming_2016_16–19_150-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ming_2016_16–19-150">[150]</a></sup> As per a <a href="/wiki/World_Health_Organization" title="World Health Organization">World Health Organization</a> (WHO) report issued in 2011, "the causes of Gender Based Violence (GBV) are multiple, but it primarily stems from gender inequality and its manifestations."<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">[151]</a></sup> The report stated: </p> 
      <dl>
       <dd>
        "In Solomon Islands, GBV has been largely normalized: 73% of men and 73% of women believe violence against women is justifiable, especially for infidelity and 'disobedience,' as when women do 'not live up to the gender roles that society imposes.' For example, women who believed they could occasionally refuse sex were four times more likely to experience GBV from an intimate partner. Men cited acceptability of violence and gender inequality as two main reasons for GBV, and almost all of them reported hitting their female partners as a 'form of discipline,' suggesting that women could improve the situation by '[learning] to obey [them].'"
       </dd>
      </dl> 
      <p>Another manifestation and driver of gender inequality in Solomon Islands is the traditional practice of <a href="/wiki/Bride_price#Solomon_Islands" title="Bride price">bride price</a>. Although specific customs vary between communities, paying a bride price is considered similar to a property title, giving men ownership over women. Gender norms of masculinity tend to encourage men to "control" their wives, often through violence, while women felt that bride prices prevented them from leaving men. Another report issued by the WHO in 2013 painted a similarly grim picture.<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">[152]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2014, Solomon Islands officially launched the Family Protection Act 2014, which was aimed at curbing domestic violence in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">[153]</a></sup> While numerous other interventions are being developed and implemented in the healthcare system as well as the criminal justice system, these interventions are still in their infancy and have largely stemmed from Western protocols. Therefore, for these models to be effective, time and commitment is needed to change the cultural perception of domestic violence in Solomon Islands.<sup id="cite_ref-Ming_2016_16–19_150-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ming_2016_16–19-150">[150]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Literature">Literature</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Solomon_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Literature">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/Solomon_Islands_literature" title="Solomon Islands literature">Solomon Islands literature</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Writers from Solomon Islands include the novelists <a href="/wiki/Rexford_Orotaloa" title="Rexford Orotaloa">Rexford Orotaloa</a> and John Saunana and the poet Jully Makini. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Solomon_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <dl>
       <dt>
        Newspapers
       </dt>
      </dl> 
      <p>There is one daily newspaper, the <i><a href="/wiki/Solomon_Star" title="Solomon Star">Solomon Star</a></i>, one daily online news website, <i>Solomon Times Online</i> (www.solomontimes.com), two weekly papers, <i>Solomons Voice</i> and <i>Solomon Times</i>, and two monthly papers, <i>Agrikalsa Nius</i> and the <i>Citizen's Press</i>. </p> 
      <dl>
       <dt>
        Radio
       </dt>
      </dl> 
      <p>Radio is the most influential type of media in Solomon Islands due to language differences, illiteracy,<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">[154]</a></sup> and the difficulty of receiving television signals in some parts of the country. The <a href="/wiki/Solomon_Islands_Broadcasting_Corporation" title="Solomon Islands Broadcasting Corporation">Solomon Islands Broadcasting Corporation</a> (SIBC) operates public radio services, including the national stations <a href="/wiki/Radio_Happy_Isles" title="Radio Happy Isles">Radio Happy Isles</a> 1037 on the dial and <a href="/wiki/Wantok_FM" title="Wantok FM">Wantok FM</a> 96.3, and the provincial stations <a href="/wiki/Radio_Happy_Lagoon" title="Radio Happy Lagoon">Radio Happy Lagoon</a> and, formerly, Radio Temotu. There are two commercial FM stations, Z FM at 99.5 in Honiara but receivable over a large majority of island out from Honiara, and, PAOA FM at 97.7 in Honiara (also broadcasting on 107.5 in Auki), and, one community FM radio station, Gold Ridge FM on 88.7. </p> 
      <dl>
       <dt>
        Television
       </dt>
      </dl> 
      <p>There are no TV services that cover the entire Solomon Islands but are available in six main centres in four of the nine Provinces. Satellite TV stations can be received. In Honiara, there is a free-to-air HD digital, analogue TV and online service called Telekom Television Limited, operated by Solomon Telekom Co. Ltd.. and rebroadcast a number of regional and international TV services including <a href="/wiki/ABC_Australia_(Southeast_Asian_TV_channel)" title="ABC Australia (Southeast Asian TV channel)">ABC Australia</a> and <a href="/wiki/BBC_World_News" title="BBC World News">BBC World News</a>. Residents can also subscribe to SATSOL, a digital pay TV service, re-transmitting satellite television. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music">Music</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Solomon_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Music">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Solomon_Islands" title="Music of Solomon Islands">Music of Solomon Islands</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Flute_de_pan_MHNT_ETH_AC_NH_31_Sav%C3%A8s.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Flute_de_pan_MHNT_ETH_AC_NH_31_Sav%C3%A8s.jpg/220px-Flute_de_pan_MHNT_ETH_AC_NH_31_Sav%C3%A8s.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="169" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Flute_de_pan_MHNT_ETH_AC_NH_31_Sav%C3%A8s.jpg/330px-Flute_de_pan_MHNT_ETH_AC_NH_31_Sav%C3%A8s.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Flute_de_pan_MHNT_ETH_AC_NH_31_Sav%C3%A8s.jpg/440px-Flute_de_pan_MHNT_ETH_AC_NH_31_Sav%C3%A8s.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5310" data-file-height="4073"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Flute_de_pan_MHNT_ETH_AC_NH_31_Sav%C3%A8s.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A pan flute, nineteenth century, <a href="/wiki/MHNT" class="mw-redirect" title="MHNT">MHNT</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Traditional <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Melanesia" title="Music of Melanesia">Melanesian music</a> in Solomon Islands includes both group and solo vocals, <a href="/wiki/Slit-drum" class="mw-redirect" title="Slit-drum">slit-drum</a> and <a href="/wiki/Panpipe" class="mw-redirect" title="Panpipe">panpipe</a> ensembles. <a href="/wiki/Bamboo_musical_instruments" title="Bamboo musical instruments">Bamboo music</a> gained a following in the 1920s. In the 1950s <a href="/wiki/Edwin_Nanau_Sitori" title="Edwin Nanau Sitori">Edwin Nanau Sitori</a> composed the song "<a href="/wiki/Walkabout_long_Chinatown" title="Walkabout long Chinatown">Walkabout long Chinatown</a>", which has been referred to by the government as the unofficial "<a href="/wiki/National_song" class="mw-redirect" title="National song">national song</a>" of the Solomon Islands.<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">[155]</a></sup> Modern Solomon Islander popular music includes various kinds of rock and reggae as well as <i>island music</i>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sport">Sport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Solomon_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: Sport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sport_in_Solomon_Islands" title="Sport in Solomon Islands">Sport in Solomon Islands</a>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Rugby_union_in_Solomon_Islands" title="Rugby union in Solomon Islands">Rugby union</a>: The <a href="/wiki/Solomon_Islands_national_rugby_union_team" title="Solomon Islands national rugby union team">Solomon Islands national rugby union team</a> has played internationals since 1969. It took part in the Oceania qualifying tournament for the 2003 and 2007 Rugby World Cups, but did not qualify on either occasion. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">Association football</a>: The <a href="/wiki/Solomon_Islands_national_football_team" title="Solomon Islands national football team">Solomon Islands national football team</a> has proved among the most successful in Oceania and is part of the OFC confederation in FIFA. They are currently ranked 141st out of 210 teams in the FIFA World Rankings. The team became the first team to beat New Zealand in qualifying for a play-off spot against Australia for qualification to the <a href="/wiki/World_Cup_2006" class="mw-redirect" title="World Cup 2006">World Cup 2006</a>. They were defeated 7–0 in Australia and 2–1 at home. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Futsal" title="Futsal">Futsal</a>: Closely related to Association Football. On 14 June 2008, the <a href="/wiki/Solomon_Islands_national_futsal_team" title="Solomon Islands national futsal team">Solomon Islands national futsal team</a>, the Kurukuru, won the Oceania Futsal Championship in Fiji to qualify them for the <a href="/wiki/2008_FIFA_Futsal_World_Cup" title="2008 FIFA Futsal World Cup">2008 FIFA Futsal World Cup</a>, which was held in Brazil from 30 September to 19 October 2008. Solomon Islands is the futsal defending champions in the Oceania region. In 2008 and 2009 the Kurukuru won the Oceania Futsal Championship in Fiji. In 2009 they defeated the host nation <a href="/wiki/Fiji" title="Fiji">Fiji</a> 8–0 to claim the title. The Kurukuru currently hold the world record for the fastest ever goal scored in an official futsal match. It was set by Kurukuru captain Elliot Ragomo, who scored against <a href="/wiki/New_Caledonia_national_futsal_team" title="New Caledonia national futsal team">New Caledonia</a> three seconds into the game in July 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">[156]</a></sup> They also, however, hold the less enviable record for the worst defeat in the history of the <a href="/wiki/FIFA_Futsal_World_Cup" title="FIFA Futsal World Cup">Futsal World Cup</a>,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (August 2018)">clarification needed</span></a></i>]</sup> when in 2008 they were beaten by <a href="/wiki/Russia_national_futsal_team" title="Russia national futsal team">Russia</a> with two goals to thirty-one.<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">[157]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Beach_soccer" title="Beach soccer">Beach soccer</a>: The <a href="/wiki/Solomon_Islands_national_beach_soccer_team" title="Solomon Islands national beach soccer team">Solomon Islands national beach soccer team</a>, the Bilikiki Boys, are statistically the most successful team in Oceania. They have won all three <a href="/wiki/FIFA_Beach_Soccer_World_Cup_qualification_(OFC)" class="mw-redirect" title="FIFA Beach Soccer World Cup qualification (OFC)">regional championships</a> to date, thereby qualifying on each occasion for the <a href="/wiki/FIFA_Beach_Soccer_World_Cup" title="FIFA Beach Soccer World Cup">FIFA Beach Soccer World Cup</a>. The Bilikiki Boys are ranked fourteenth in the world as of 2010<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Solomon_Islands&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, higher than any other team from Oceania.<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">[158]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Solomon_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
